Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do instantaneous letters have eternal possibility but not possibility of eternal existence?
A) Because they exist only in the instant of their occurrence.
B) Because they are non-stationary.
C) Because their quiddity requires passing away after existence.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Non-stationary entities demonstrate that eternal possibility does not entail eternal existence, because they are possible in each moment but cannot continue.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You exist right now, but every moment of your existence is a new creation by Allah. If your essence required passing away like an instantaneous letter, you would cease. Does the fact that Allah sustains you from moment to moment humble you, or do you still feel self-sufficient? What would change if you lived with the constant awareness that you are non-stationary without His power?
?
The commentator assumed a general rule without considering exceptions. Do you have any comfortable beliefs about your own permanence or continuity that you have never verified in light of revelation? Take one such belief and examine it: is it a truth or an assumption?
?
If your quiddity (essence) required passing away after existence, you would have no hope of continuing. Yet Allah promises eternal life to the believers. How does this distinction between impossibility for creation and possibility for the Creator reshape your trust in Allah's promise? Do you live as if you really believe He can give you eternal life, or do you doubt His power?

Eternal Possibility Does Not Guarantee Simultaneous Existence
Al-Iji presents the logical proof and its critique regarding eternal possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that a thing's possibility being eternal and continuous in every part of eternity does not logically necessitate its existence in all parts simultaneously.

Core Idea
Eternal possibility in each part does not guarantee simultaneous existence in all.

This lesson examines a subtle logical argument about possibility and eternity. The author presents a claim that if a thing's possibility is eternal and continuous, its essence cannot prevent existence in any part of eternity. However, he then shows that this reasoning only establishes possibility in each part individually (badalan) but not in all parts together (ma'an). Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating arguments about the eternal existence of possible beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical flow: argument, explanation, critique.
2
Identify the initial claim and its support
Locate the statement that eternal possibility implies absence of prevention in each part. Understand how the commentator explains this: if the essence were a preventer in any part, possibility would not be continuous.
3
Understand the objection: badal vs. ma'a
The passage argues that even if eternal possibility allows existence in each part individually (badal), it does not allow existence in all parts simultaneously (ma'a). Grasp why the general does not entail the specific.
The objection uses the terms badal (substitute) and ma'a (together).
4
Reflect on the logical principle
Consider the principle: the entailer of a general is not necessarily an entailer of the specific. Apply this to the argument.
5
Test your understanding with the checkpoint
Answer the multiple-choice question to confirm you can distinguish between the two types of possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبول الوجود في شيء من أجزاء الأزل، فيكون عدم منعه منه أمراً مستمراً في جميع تلك الأجزاء، فإذا نظرا إلى ذاته من حيث هو لم يمنع من اتصافه بالوجود في شيء
قوله : ( إمكانه إذا كان مستمراً أزلياً إلخ) أي إذا كان جميع أجزاء الأزل ظرفاً للإمكان . قوله : (لم يكن هو في ذاته مانعاً إلخ) أي يكون الازل ظرفاً لعدم المنع، أي لم تكن ذاته في شيء من أجزاء الأزل مانعاً عن قبول الوجود، إذ لو كان في شيء منها مانعاً عنه انتفى إمكانه في ذلك الجزء، لأن عدم المنع لازم للإمكان. وانتفاء اللازم يستلزم انتفاء الملزوم، فلا يكون الإمكان مستمراً في جميع أجزاء الأزل . قوله : ( فيكون إلخ) أي إذا كان الأزل ظرفاً لعدم المنع يكون عدم منعه أجزاء الأزل، بحيث لا يشذ منها جزء، فيكون الأزل ظرفاً لاستمرار عدم منعه .
مستمراً في جميع
قوله : ( فإذا نظر إلخ يعني استمرار عدم المنع في جميع أجزاء الأزل بحيث لا يخرج منها جزء يستلزم عدم المنع من الاتصاف بالوجود في شيء منها، على أن يكون في شيء منها ظرف الجملة، وليس في كلامه ما يستلزم جواز هذا أصلاً، وأبعد منه ما ضمه إليه من قوله : لا بدلاً فقط، بل ومعاً أيضاً، فإنه لو سلم أن أزلية الإمكان يستلزم جواز الاتصاف بالوجود في كل جزء من أجزاء الأزل، فمن أين يلزم جواز المقارنة ؟ ومعلوم أن الاتصاف بالوجود في كل جزء من أجزاء الأزل أعم من الاتصاف به في كل منها معاً، ومستلزم العام لا يجب أن يكون مستلزماً للخاص. فقوله : وجواز اتصافه به في كل منها معاً إلخ أن الذي فرع عليه ما زعمه من استلزام أزلية الإمكان لإمكان الأزلية مما لا طائل تحته. انتهى كلامه.
The acceptance of existence in some part of eternity, so the absence of prevention from it is a continuous matter in all those parts. When we consider its essence as such, it does not prevent its being characterized by existence in any part. His saying: (its possibility if it is continuous eternally etc.) i.e., if all parts of eternity are the locus of possibility. His saying: (it is not in itself a preventer etc.) i.e., eternity is the locus of the absence of prevention, i.e., its essence is not in any part of eternity a preventer from accepting existence, because if it were a preventer in some part, its possibility would be negated in that part, since the absence of prevention is necessary for possibility. The negation of the necessary entails the negation of that which necessitates, so possibility would not be continuous in all parts of eternity. His saying: (so it becomes etc.) i.e., if eternity is the locus of the absence of prevention, then the absence of prevention from it is in all parts of eternity such that no part is excluded, so eternity is the locus of the continuity of the absence of prevention. His saying: (so if we consider etc.) means the continuity of the absence of prevention in all parts of eternity such that no part is excluded entails the absence of prevention from being characterized by existence in some part, such that some part is the locus of the sentence. There is nothing in his speech that entails the permissibility of this at all, and more far-fetched is what he included from his saying: not only as a substitute, but also together. For if we grant that the eternity of possibility entails the permissibility of being characterized by existence in every part of eternity, from where does the permissibility of simultaneity follow? It is known that being characterized by existence in every part of eternity is more general than being characterized by it in all of them together, and the entailer of the general is not necessarily an entailer of the specific. So his saying: and the permissibility of being characterized by it in all of them together etc. shows that what he based his claim of the eternity of possibility entailing the possibility of eternity is baseless. End of his speech.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents a logical argument about the relationship between eternal possibility (imkan azali) and the possibility of eternity (imkan al-azaliyya). It is part of a commentary on a statement that if a possible thing's possibility is eternal and continuous in all parts of eternity, then its essence does not prevent existence in any part. The author explains that if the essence were a preventer in any part, possibility would not be continuous. The key point comes when the author discusses the difference between the permissibility of existence in each part separately (badalan) and in all parts simultaneously (ma'an). He argues that even if eternal possibility entails permissibility in each part individually, it does not necessarily entail permissibility in all parts together, because the entailer of a general thing does not entail the specific. Therefore, the claim that eternal possibility entails the possibility of eternal existence (simultaneous) is not proven. The passage ends with 'End of his speech,' indicating a conclusion.

إمكان
أزل
بدلية
معية
امتناع
لازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if a thing can exist in every part of eternity individually, it can also exist in all parts together simultaneously.
Correction: The passage clarifies that this is not logically necessary: the general (existence in each part individually) does not entail the specific (existence in all parts together).

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between the permissibility of existence in each part of eternity and the permissibility of existence in all parts simultaneously according to the passage?
A) The former entails the latter necessarily.
B) The latter is more general and not entailed by the former.
C) They are equivalent.
D) The former is impossible.

Key Takeaway
Eternal possibility does not logically necessitate simultaneous eternal existence; the general does not entail the specific.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own aspirations, do you often assume that because something is possible step by step, it will happen all at once? How does this logical lesson about the general not entailing the specific recalibrate your expectations of God's timing?
?
If logical possibility does not guarantee actuality, how does that affect your sense of reliance on God? When you pray for something possible, do you still hold tightly to the outcome, or do you truly submit to God's will?
?
This passage shows that even the absence of prevention does not force existence. Where in your life have you assumed that lack of obstacles means something should happen? What would it mean to trust God's wisdom even when possibilities remain unrealized?

Essential Possibility and Impossibility by Another
Al-Iji explains the distinction between essential possibility and accidental impossibility, using the example of a temporal event.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between essential possibility (imkan dhati) and impossibility due to an external condition (imtina' bi al-ghayr), and why one does not negate the other.

Core Idea
A thing can be possible in itself yet impossible in relation to another.

The passage introduces a subtle but crucial distinction: a thing's possibility relative to its own essence is not invalidated by impossibility that arises from something external. This forms the backbone of al-Iji's reply to objections about the eternity of possible entities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how the author distinguishes between possibility by essence and impossibility by another.
Pay special attention to the phrase 'لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي'.
2
Identify the two types of impossibility
The passage mentions two kinds: impossibility due to a necessary description (like being instantaneous) and impossibility due to temporal restriction. See how each relates to essential possibility.
Consider the example of the temporal event (hadith) taken alone vs. taken with the condition of temporality.
3
Reflect on the philosophical implications
Think about why this distinction matters for arguments about the eternity of the world. It shows that even if something cannot be eternal due to an external factor, its essence remains possible.
This will be used later in responses to objections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن ما ذكره الشارح المحقق منقوض إجمالاً بالزمان والحركة؛ لأن ممكن الوجود منهما عند المحققين هو الآن السيال، والحركة بمعنى التوسط، وهما أمران قاران لا أجزاء لهما أصلاً، فإمكانهما أزلي وأزليتهما ممكنة، بل واقعة عند الفلاسفة. وأما الحركة بمعنى القطع والزمان الغير القار فلا إمكان لهما أصلاً، ولا بمقولة الفعل والانفعال، فإن الشارح قرر الاستدلال على امتناعهما ولم يجب عنه فلعلهما عنده غير موجودين، هو مذهب متأخري المحققين بل الحروف الآنية التي تعرض للأصوات عند انقطاعها كعروض الآن للزمان والنقطة للخط، إذ قد صرحوا وصرح الشارح أيضا بأنها ليس لها وجود إلا في آن حدوثها، فلها أزلية الإمكان دون إمكان الأزلية والقول بأن أزليتها ممكنة نظراً إليها ذاتها وماهيتها والامتناع بالنظر إلى الغير أعني الوجود في الزمان الأول مما لا يلتفت إليه؛ لأن هذا الغير متحقق على تقدير استمرار وجودها فإذا اقتضى ماهياتها التقضي بعد الوجود لم يمكن لها لذاتها استمرار ،قطعاً، كما لا يخفى على المتأمل. اللهم إلا أن يجوز أن يكون عدم تصور استمرارها لأمر خارج عن ماهياتها على أن لك أن تجعل صورة النقض سنداً للمنع، ويمكن أن يتخلص من النقض بمنع إمكان شيء غير ،قار، وتوضيحه أن الشارح الآن بصدد دفع ما ذكره القوم من قولهم : أزلية الإمكان غير مستلزم لإمكان الأزلية وجواباً عن التشكيك على قولهم : الإمكان لازم لماهية الممكن فهو بهذا البحث مؤيد للتشكيك فلم يتحقق بعد أزلية إمكان كل ممكن، ولا شبهة أن ورود النقض موقوف على ثبوت أزلية إمكان للأمر الغير القار، فللمناظر أن كما
منها، بل جاز اتصافه به في كل منها، لا بدلاً فقط، بل ومعاً أيضاً. وجواز اتصافه به في كل منها معاً هو إمكان اتصافه بالوجود المستمر في جميع أجزاء الأزل بالنظر إلى ذاته، فأزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية. نعم ربما امتنعت الأزلية بسبب الغير، وذلك لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي، مثلاً الحادث يمكن أزليته بالنظر إلى ذاته من حيث هو، ويمتنع إذا أخذ الحادث مقيداً بحدوثه فذات الحادث من حيث هو إمكانه أزلي، وأزليته ممكنة أيضاً، وإذا أخذ مع قيد الحدوث لم يكن لهذا المجموع إمكان أصلاً، لأن الحدوث أمر اعتباري يستحيل وجوده فالمجموع من حيث هو ممتنع لا ممكن. فإن قلت : نحن نأخذ ذات الحادث لا وحده بل مع الحدوث، على أنه قيد لا جزء . . ونقول : إنه ممتنع في الأزل وممكن فيما لا يزال . قلت : الإمكان الذاتي معتبر بالقياس إلى ذات الشيء من حيث هو، فإن أخذ ذات الحادث وحده، أو ذات
الاتصاف بالوجود إذ لو تحقق المنع من الاتصاف بالوجود في الجزء لم يكن عدم المنع عن قبول الوجود مستمراً، لأن قبول الوجود هو الاتصاف به.
قوله : (بل جاز اتصافه إلخ لأن عدم المنع عن الاتصاف يستلزم جواز الاتصاف، فيجوز الاتصاف بالوجود في كل جزء منها، بأن يكون كل جزء منها ظرفاً للاتصاف . قوله : ( لا بد له فقط بل ومعاً أيضاً لأن كل جزء منها مع قطع النظر عن جزء آخر يكون ظرفاً للاتصاف، على ما هو معنى الكل الإفرادي، فيكون شاملاً للاتصاف بطريق البدلية، بأن يكون كل جزء بدلاً عن الآخر في الاتصاف، وللاتصاف بطريق المعية بأن يكون كل جزء مجتمعاً مع جزء آخر في الاتصاف، فيكون الاتصاف بالوجود حاصلاً في جميعها، وهو الاتصاف بالوجود المستمر فجوازه جوازه. وبما حررنا ظهر الملازمات في جميع الشرطيات واندفع المنوع التي أوردها الناظرون، فلا حاجة إلى الإطناب ولا يرد عليه النقص بالحروف الآنية، ولا المنع بجعلها سنداً على ما ،وهم لأن أزليتها بالنظر إلى ماهياتها ممكنة وإن كانت ممتنعة بالنظر إلى وصف لازم لذاتها، أعني كونها آنية فإنه لا تنافي بين إمكان الشيء بالقياس إلى ذاته، وامتناعه بالقياس إلى أمر لازم لذاته، فتدبر
قوله : ( نعم إلخ) تقرير لما سبق، وجواب عن التشكيك المذكور بطريق آخر بمنع أن أزلية الحوادث غير ممكنة في الأزل؛ لأن الامتناع بسبب الحدوث امتناع ،بالغير، وهو لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي .
يقول : كما أنه لا يجوز اتصاف الأمر الغير القار بالوجود في أجزاء الأزل معاً، ليس له أيضاً إمكان مستمر فيها .
قوله : نعم ربما امتنعت إلخ) جواب عن سؤال مقدر ، وبه يخرج الجواب عن التشكيك ابتداء . قوله: (قلت : الإمكان الذاتي إلخ) قيد الإمكان بالذاتي احترازاً عن الإمكان الاستعدادي، لا عن الإمكان بالغير.
Then what the verifying commentator mentioned is refuted in general by time and motion; because what is possible in existence from them according to the verifiers is the flowing now and motion in the sense of intermediateness, and they are two settled things with no parts at all, so their possibility is eternal and their eternity is possible, indeed actual according to the philosophers. As for motion in the sense of traversing and non-settled time, they have no possibility at all, nor in the category of action and passion, for the commentator established the proof of their impossibility and did not answer it; perhaps they are non-existent according to him; this is the school of later verifiers. Rather, the instantaneous letters that occur to sounds when they are cut off, like the occurrence of the now to time and the point to the line, for they have stated and the commentator has also stated that they have no existence except in the instant of their occurrence, so they have the eternity of possibility without the possibility of eternity. And the statement that their eternity is possible in view of their essence and quiddity, and the impossibility in view of the other, meaning existence in the first time, is not to be heeded; because this other is realized on the assumption of the continuation of their existence, so if their quiddities require passing away after existence, they cannot have continuance in themselves, decisively, as is not hidden from the contemplative. Unless it is permissible that the non-imagination of their continuance is due to something external to their quiddities, such that you may make the image of the refutation a support for prevention, and it is possible to extricate from the refutation by preventing the possibility of something non-settled. And its clarification is that the commentator is now in the process of repelling what the people mentioned from their statement: the eternity of possibility does not entail the possibility of eternity, and answering the doubt concerning their statement: possibility is necessary for the quiddity of the possible, so he is by this research supporting the doubt; so the eternity of possibility of every possible has not been established, and there is no doubt that the arrival of the refutation is dependent on establishing the eternity of possibility for the non-settled thing, so the disputant has that...
From them, rather it is permissible for it to be characterized by it in each of them, not only as a substitute, but also together. And the permissibility of its being characterized by it in each of them together is the possibility of its being characterized by continuous existence in all parts of eternity with respect to its essence, so the eternity of possibility entails the possibility of eternity. Yes, perhaps eternity is prevented due to another, and that does not contradict essential possibility. For example, an occurrence (hadith) can be eternal with respect to its essence as such, and is impossible if the occurrence is taken as restricted by its temporality; so the essence of the occurrence as such its possibility is eternal, and its eternity is also possible. And if taken with the condition of temporality, this composite has no possibility at all, because temporality is an adventitious thing whose existence is impossible, so the composite as such is impossible, not possible. For if you say: we take the essence of the occurrence not alone but with temporality, as a condition not a part... and we say: it is impossible in eternity and possible in what is not yet. I say: essential possibility is considered with respect to the essence of the thing as such, for if the essence of the occurrence is taken alone, or the essence...
Being characterized by existence, for if prevention from being characterized by existence were realized in the part, then the absence of prevention from accepting existence would not be continuous, because accepting existence is being characterized by it.
His saying: (rather it is permissible for it to be characterized etc.) because the absence of prevention from being characterized entails the permissibility of being characterized, so it is permissible to be characterized by existence in every part of them, such that every part is a locus of characterization. His saying: (not only as a substitute but also together) because every part of them, irrespective of another part, is a locus of characterization, according to the meaning of the individual whole, so it includes characterization by way of substitution, such that each part is a substitute for another in characterization, and characterization by way of togetherness, such that each part is combined with another part in characterization, so characterization by existence occurs in all of them, which is characterization by continuous existence, so its permissibility is its permissibility. And by what we have explained, the entailments in all conditionals become manifest, and the preventions that the disputants mentioned are repelled, so there is no need for prolixity. And the objection from instantaneous letters does not apply, nor the prevention by making them a support for what they imagined, because their eternity with respect to their quiddities is possible, even if they are impossible with respect to a description necessary to their essence, namely being instantaneous. For there is no contradiction between the possibility of a thing with respect to its essence and its impossibility with respect to something necessary to its essence, so ponder.
His saying: (Yes etc.) is a confirmation of what preceded, and an answer to the mentioned doubt by another way, by preventing that the eternity of events is impossible in eternity; because the impossibility due to temporality is an impossibility by another, and it does not contradict essential possibility.
He says: Just as it is not permissible for the non-settled thing to be characterized by existence in parts of eternity together, it also does not have continuous possibility in them.
His saying: (Yes, perhaps it is prevented etc.) is an answer to an implied question, and by it the answer to the doubt emerges initially. His saying: (I said: essential possibility etc.) restricts possibility to essential possibility to avoid the sense of dispositional possibility, not possibility by another.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer sequence. The objection is raised that the earlier proof is refuted by time and motion, because certain entities (like the flowing now and motion as intermediation) are settled and have no parts, so they have eternal possibility and their eternity is actual. Other entities (traversing motion and non-settled time) are impossible, and the commentator did not answer this, perhaps because he denies them. Also instantaneous letters (huruf aniyya) only exist in the instant of their occurrence, so they have the eternity of possibility but not the possibility of eternity. The author responds by distinguishing essential possibility from accidental impossibility. He explains that even if an entity like an occurrence (hadith) is impossible in eternity when taken with the condition of temporality, its essence alone has eternal possibility. The key point is that possibility with respect to the essence does not contradict impossibility due to an external condition or a necessary attribute (like being instantaneous). The commentator's remarks reinforce this: the eternity of events is not impossible in eternity because the impossibility is by another (bi al-ghayr), not by essence. Thus essential possibility (imkan dhati) remains unaffected. The passage concludes that there is no contradiction between the possibility of a thing in itself and its impossibility due to something necessary to its essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If something is impossible in eternity, it cannot be essentially possible.
Correction: The passage shows that impossibility due to an external condition (e.g., temporality) does not affect essential possibility.

Checkpoint
What does al-Iji use to illustrate the distinction between essential possibility and impossibility by another?
A) The example of time and motion.
B) The example of a temporal event (hadith).
C) The example of instantaneous letters.
D) The example of a continuous line.

Key Takeaway
Essential possibility is not canceled by impossibility arising from an external condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely considered some of your shortcomings as permanent parts of who you are. But according to this lesson, what if they are merely accidental conditions that do not define your essence? Will you allow a condition, rather than your essential capacity, to dictate your potential for change?
?
The objection in the passage confuses a condition with a part of the essence. In your life, do you ever treat temporary failures as if they are essential to your identity? How can you apply the distinction from this lesson to separate your core self from passing circumstances?
?
If essential possibility can never be destroyed by external impossibility, what does that mean for your hope in divine mercy? Is there any sin or state that can make you essentially incapable of returning to God? How does this lesson strengthen your trust in His acceptance of repentance?

Rational Judgments
intermediate
5 min
Responding to the Objection from Non-Continuous Entities
Al-Iji presents and answers an objection based on non-continuous entities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Iji refutes the objection that non-settled entities like time, motion, and instantaneous letters cannot have eternal possibility.

Core Idea
Even if actual eternity is impossible for some entities, their essential possibility remains eternal.

The objection claims that entities which exist only momentarily (like instantaneous letters) cannot have eternal possibility. Al-Iji responds by again appealing to the distinction between essential and accidental impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Find the part where the objector mentions time, motion in two senses, and instantaneous letters. Understand why they think these entities undermine the earlier proof.
The objector is using these examples to challenge the claim that all possibles have eternal possibility.
2
Identify al-Iji's response
Al-Iji responds by showing that even if such entities cannot be eternal due to their nature (e.g., they are non-settled), their possibility with respect to their essence is still eternal.
Key phrase: 'فلا تنافي بين إمكان الشيء بالقياس إلى ذاته وامتناعه بالقياس إلى أمر لازم لذاته'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this response defends the original proof. The objector's examples do not refute the eternity of essential possibility; they only show that some things are impossible by another.
This reinforces the core distinction from the previous lesson.

ثم إن ما ذكره الشارح المحقق منقوض إجمالاً بالزمان والحركة؛ لأن ممكن الوجود منهما عند المحققين هو الآن السيال، والحركة بمعنى التوسط، وهما أمران قاران لا أجزاء لهما أصلاً، فإمكانهما أزلي وأزليتهما ممكنة، بل واقعة عند الفلاسفة. وأما الحركة بمعنى القطع والزمان الغير القار فلا إمكان لهما أصلاً، ولا بمقولة الفعل والانفعال، فإن الشارح قرر الاستدلال على امتناعهما ولم يجب عنه فلعلهما عنده غير موجودين، هو مذهب متأخري المحققين بل الحروف الآنية التي تعرض للأصوات عند انقطاعها كعروض الآن للزمان والنقطة للخط، إذ قد صرحوا وصرح الشارح أيضا بأنها ليس لها وجود إلا في آن حدوثها، فلها أزلية الإمكان دون إمكان الأزلية والقول بأن أزليتها ممكنة نظراً إليها ذاتها وماهيتها والامتناع بالنظر إلى الغير أعني الوجود في الزمان الأول مما لا يلتفت إليه؛ لأن هذا الغير متحقق على تقدير استمرار وجودها فإذا اقتضى ماهياتها التقضي بعد الوجود لم يمكن لها لذاتها استمرار ،قطعاً، كما لا يخفى على المتأمل. اللهم إلا أن يجوز أن يكون عدم تصور استمرارها لأمر خارج عن ماهياتها على أن لك أن تجعل صورة النقض سنداً للمنع، ويمكن أن يتخلص من النقض بمنع إمكان شيء غير ،قار، وتوضيحه أن الشارح الآن بصدد دفع ما ذكره القوم من قولهم : أزلية الإمكان غير مستلزم لإمكان الأزلية وجواباً عن التشكيك على قولهم : الإمكان لازم لماهية الممكن فهو بهذا البحث مؤيد للتشكيك فلم يتحقق بعد أزلية إمكان كل ممكن، ولا شبهة أن ورود النقض موقوف على ثبوت أزلية إمكان للأمر الغير القار، فللمناظر أن كما
منها، بل جاز اتصافه به في كل منها، لا بدلاً فقط، بل ومعاً أيضاً. وجواز اتصافه به في كل منها معاً هو إمكان اتصافه بالوجود المستمر في جميع أجزاء الأزل بالنظر إلى ذاته، فأزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية. نعم ربما امتنعت الأزلية بسبب الغير، وذلك لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي، مثلاً الحادث يمكن أزليته بالنظر إلى ذاته من حيث هو، ويمتنع إذا أخذ الحادث مقيداً بحدوثه فذات الحادث من حيث هو إمكانه أزلي، وأزليته ممكنة أيضاً، وإذا أخذ مع قيد الحدوث لم يكن لهذا المجموع إمكان أصلاً، لأن الحدوث أمر اعتباري يستحيل وجوده فالمجموع من حيث هو ممتنع لا ممكن. فإن قلت : نحن نأخذ ذات الحادث لا وحده بل مع الحدوث، على أنه قيد لا جزء . . ونقول : إنه ممتنع في الأزل وممكن فيما لا يزال . قلت : الإمكان الذاتي معتبر بالقياس إلى ذات الشيء من حيث هو، فإن أخذ ذات الحادث وحده، أو ذات
الاتصاف بالوجود إذ لو تحقق المنع من الاتصاف بالوجود في الجزء لم يكن عدم المنع عن قبول الوجود مستمراً، لأن قبول الوجود هو الاتصاف به.
قوله : (بل جاز اتصافه إلخ لأن عدم المنع عن الاتصاف يستلزم جواز الاتصاف، فيجوز الاتصاف بالوجود في كل جزء منها، بأن يكون كل جزء منها ظرفاً للاتصاف . قوله : ( لا بد له فقط بل ومعاً أيضاً لأن كل جزء منها مع قطع النظر عن جزء آخر يكون ظرفاً للاتصاف، على ما هو معنى الكل الإفرادي، فيكون شاملاً للاتصاف بطريق البدلية، بأن يكون كل جزء بدلاً عن الآخر في الاتصاف، وللاتصاف بطريق المعية بأن يكون كل جزء مجتمعاً مع جزء آخر في الاتصاف، فيكون الاتصاف بالوجود حاصلاً في جميعها، وهو الاتصاف بالوجود المستمر فجوازه جوازه. وبما حررنا ظهر الملازمات في جميع الشرطيات واندفع المنوع التي أوردها الناظرون، فلا حاجة إلى الإطناب ولا يرد عليه النقص بالحروف الآنية، ولا المنع بجعلها سنداً على ما ،وهم لأن أزليتها بالنظر إلى ماهياتها ممكنة وإن كانت ممتنعة بالنظر إلى وصف لازم لذاتها، أعني كونها آنية فإنه لا تنافي بين إمكان الشيء بالقياس إلى ذاته، وامتناعه بالقياس إلى أمر لازم لذاته، فتدبر
قوله : ( نعم إلخ) تقرير لما سبق، وجواب عن التشكيك المذكور بطريق آخر بمنع أن أزلية الحوادث غير ممكنة في الأزل؛ لأن الامتناع بسبب الحدوث امتناع ،بالغير، وهو لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي .
يقول : كما أنه لا يجوز اتصاف الأمر الغير القار بالوجود في أجزاء الأزل معاً، ليس له أيضاً إمكان مستمر فيها .
قوله : نعم ربما امتنعت إلخ) جواب عن سؤال مقدر ، وبه يخرج الجواب عن التشكيك ابتداء . قوله: (قلت : الإمكان الذاتي إلخ) قيد الإمكان بالذاتي احترازاً عن الإمكان الاستعدادي، لا عن الإمكان بالغير.
Then what the verifying commentator mentioned is refuted in general by time and motion; because what is possible in existence from them according to the verifiers is the flowing now and motion in the sense of intermediateness, and they are two settled things with no parts at all, so their possibility is eternal and their eternity is possible, indeed actual according to the philosophers. As for motion in the sense of traversing and non-settled time, they have no possibility at all, nor in the category of action and passion, for the commentator established the proof of their impossibility and did not answer it; perhaps they are non-existent according to him; this is the school of later verifiers. Rather, the instantaneous letters that occur to sounds when they are cut off, like the occurrence of the now to time and the point to the line, for they have stated and the commentator has also stated that they have no existence except in the instant of their occurrence, so they have the eternity of possibility without the possibility of eternity. And the statement that their eternity is possible in view of their essence and quiddity, and the impossibility in view of the other, meaning existence in the first time, is not to be heeded; because this other is realized on the assumption of the continuation of their existence, so if their quiddities require passing away after existence, they cannot have continuance in themselves, decisively, as is not hidden from the contemplative. Unless it is permissible that the non-imagination of their continuance is due to something external to their quiddities, such that you may make the image of the refutation a support for prevention, and it is possible to extricate from the refutation by preventing the possibility of something non-settled. And its clarification is that the commentator is now in the process of repelling what the people mentioned from their statement: the eternity of possibility does not entail the possibility of eternity, and answering the doubt concerning their statement: possibility is necessary for the quiddity of the possible, so he is by this research supporting the doubt; so the eternity of possibility of every possible has not been established, and there is no doubt that the arrival of the refutation is dependent on establishing the eternity of possibility for the non-settled thing, so the disputant has that...
From them, rather it is permissible for it to be characterized by it in each of them, not only as a substitute, but also together. And the permissibility of its being characterized by it in each of them together is the possibility of its being characterized by continuous existence in all parts of eternity with respect to its essence, so the eternity of possibility entails the possibility of eternity. Yes, perhaps eternity is prevented due to another, and that does not contradict essential possibility. For example, an occurrence (hadith) can be eternal with respect to its essence as such, and is impossible if the occurrence is taken as restricted by its temporality; so the essence of the occurrence as such its possibility is eternal, and its eternity is also possible. And if taken with the condition of temporality, this composite has no possibility at all, because temporality is an adventitious thing whose existence is impossible, so the composite as such is impossible, not possible. For if you say: we take the essence of the occurrence not alone but with temporality, as a condition not a part... and we say: it is impossible in eternity and possible in what is not yet. I say: essential possibility is considered with respect to the essence of the thing as such, for if the essence of the occurrence is taken alone, or the essence...
Being characterized by existence, for if prevention from being characterized by existence were realized in the part, then the absence of prevention from accepting existence would not be continuous, because accepting existence is being characterized by it.
His saying: (rather it is permissible for it to be characterized etc.) because the absence of prevention from being characterized entails the permissibility of being characterized, so it is permissible to be characterized by existence in every part of them, such that every part is a locus of characterization. His saying: (not only as a substitute but also together) because every part of them, irrespective of another part, is a locus of characterization, according to the meaning of the individual whole, so it includes characterization by way of substitution, such that each part is a substitute for another in characterization, and characterization by way of togetherness, such that each part is combined with another part in characterization, so characterization by existence occurs in all of them, which is characterization by continuous existence, so its permissibility is its permissibility. And by what we have explained, the entailments in all conditionals become manifest, and the preventions that the disputants mentioned are repelled, so there is no need for prolixity. And the objection from instantaneous letters does not apply, nor the prevention by making them a support for what they imagined, because their eternity with respect to their quiddities is possible, even if they are impossible with respect to a description necessary to their essence, namely being instantaneous. For there is no contradiction between the possibility of a thing with respect to its essence and its impossibility with respect to something necessary to its essence, so ponder.
His saying: (Yes etc.) is a confirmation of what preceded, and an answer to the mentioned doubt by another way, by preventing that the eternity of events is impossible in eternity; because the impossibility due to temporality is an impossibility by another, and it does not contradict essential possibility.
He says: Just as it is not permissible for the non-settled thing to be characterized by existence in parts of eternity together, it also does not have continuous possibility in them.
His saying: (Yes, perhaps it is prevented etc.) is an answer to an implied question, and by it the answer to the doubt emerges initially. His saying: (I said: essential possibility etc.) restricts possibility to essential possibility to avoid the sense of dispositional possibility, not possibility by another.

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer sequence. The objection is raised that the earlier proof is refuted by time and motion, because certain entities (like the flowing now and motion as intermediation) are settled and have no parts, so they have eternal possibility and their eternity is actual. Other entities (traversing motion and non-settled time) are impossible, and the commentator did not answer this, perhaps because he denies them. Also instantaneous letters (huruf aniyya) only exist in the instant of their occurrence, so they have the eternity of possibility but not the possibility of eternity. The author responds by distinguishing essential possibility from accidental impossibility. He explains that even if an entity like an occurrence (hadith) is impossible in eternity when taken with the condition of temporality, its essence alone has eternal possibility. The key point is that possibility with respect to the essence does not contradict impossibility due to an external condition or a necessary attribute (like being instantaneous). The commentator's remarks reinforce this: the eternity of events is not impossible in eternity because the impossibility is by another (bi al-ghayr), not by essence. Thus essential possibility (imkan dhati) remains unaffected. The passage concludes that there is no contradiction between the possibility of a thing in itself and its impossibility due to something necessary to its essence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If an entity can only exist momentarily, then it cannot have eternal possibility in any sense.
Correction: The passage shows that such entities still have eternal essential possibility, even if actual eternal existence is impossible.

Checkpoint
What do instantaneous letters (al-huruf al-aniyya) have according to the passage?
A) They have no possibility at all.
B) They have the possibility of eternity but not the eternity of possibility.
C) They have the eternity of possibility but not the possibility of eternity.
D) They have both.

Key Takeaway
Non-continuous entities do not undermine the eternity of essential possibility; they only show that some impossibilities are due to external conditions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a flaw or weakness in your character that you have struggled with for years. According to this lesson, does the fact that it has persisted mean it is impossible for you to change? What is the difference between the essential possibility of being otherwise and the external constraints you have accepted? Will you now act on that possibility, or continue to treat your flaw as inevitable?
?
The passage teaches that even something that only exists for an instant has eternal possibility. Consider a good deed you did that felt small or fleeting—did you dismiss it as insignificant? How does the concept of eternal possibility give weight to even momentary acts of faith? How can you let this truth motivate you to seize every instant for goodness, knowing its possibility is timeless before Allah?
?
The author distinguishes between essential possibility and impossibility due to external factors. Is there a fear or doubt that you have attributed to your own nature—thinking 'I could never do that'—that might actually be an external obstacle you have assumed was intrinsic? What would it mean for your life if you separated your essential potential from those perceived limitations? What step will you take today to act on that essential possibility?

The Entailment: Eternal Possibility and Possibility of Eternity
Al-Iji explains the entailment between eternal possibility and possibility of eternity, with qualifications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the entailment from eternal possibility to possibility of eternity holds for the essence alone, and how external conditions like temporality block it.

Core Idea
Eternal possibility entails possibility of eternity for the essence, but not when the thing is taken with a condition.

This lesson focuses on the logical relationship between 'eternity of possibility' and 'possibility of eternity'. The passage explains that the entailment holds when considering the essence, but is overridden by external conditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the entailment statement
Find the sentence: 'فأزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية'. Understand what it means: if something has the property of being possible eternally, then it is possible for it to be eternal.
This is a key logical move in the argument.
2
See the qualification
The author immediately adds: 'نعم ربما امتنعت الأزلية بسبب الغير'. This shows that the entailment is valid only for essential possibility, not when another factor intervenes.
The hadith example illustrates this qualification.
3
Contrast with the objector's view
The objector denied the entailment. Al-Iji shows it holds for the essence, but the objector mistakenly considered the thing with its condition.
This clarifies the confusion.

ثم إن ما ذكره الشارح المحقق منقوض إجمالاً بالزمان والحركة؛ لأن ممكن الوجود منهما عند المحققين هو الآن السيال، والحركة بمعنى التوسط، وهما أمران قاران لا أجزاء لهما أصلاً، فإمكانهما أزلي وأزليتهما ممكنة، بل واقعة عند الفلاسفة. وأما الحركة بمعنى القطع والزمان الغير القار فلا إمكان لهما أصلاً، ولا بمقولة الفعل والانفعال، فإن الشارح قرر الاستدلال على امتناعهما ولم يجب عنه فلعلهما عنده غير موجودين، هو مذهب متأخري المحققين بل الحروف الآنية التي تعرض للأصوات عند انقطاعها كعروض الآن للزمان والنقطة للخط، إذ قد صرحوا وصرح الشارح أيضا بأنها ليس لها وجود إلا في آن حدوثها، فلها أزلية الإمكان دون إمكان الأزلية والقول بأن أزليتها ممكنة نظراً إليها ذاتها وماهيتها والامتناع بالنظر إلى الغير أعني الوجود في الزمان الأول مما لا يلتفت إليه؛ لأن هذا الغير متحقق على تقدير استمرار وجودها فإذا اقتضى ماهياتها التقضي بعد الوجود لم يمكن لها لذاتها استمرار ،قطعاً، كما لا يخفى على المتأمل. اللهم إلا أن يجوز أن يكون عدم تصور استمرارها لأمر خارج عن ماهياتها على أن لك أن تجعل صورة النقض سنداً للمنع، ويمكن أن يتخلص من النقض بمنع إمكان شيء غير ،قار، وتوضيحه أن الشارح الآن بصدد دفع ما ذكره القوم من قولهم : أزلية الإمكان غير مستلزم لإمكان الأزلية وجواباً عن التشكيك على قولهم : الإمكان لازم لماهية الممكن فهو بهذا البحث مؤيد للتشكيك فلم يتحقق بعد أزلية إمكان كل ممكن، ولا شبهة أن ورود النقض موقوف على ثبوت أزلية إمكان للأمر الغير القار، فللمناظر أن كما
منها، بل جاز اتصافه به في كل منها، لا بدلاً فقط، بل ومعاً أيضاً. وجواز اتصافه به في كل منها معاً هو إمكان اتصافه بالوجود المستمر في جميع أجزاء الأزل بالنظر إلى ذاته، فأزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية. نعم ربما امتنعت الأزلية بسبب الغير، وذلك لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي، مثلاً الحادث يمكن أزليته بالنظر إلى ذاته من حيث هو، ويمتنع إذا أخذ الحادث مقيداً بحدوثه فذات الحادث من حيث هو إمكانه أزلي، وأزليته ممكنة أيضاً، وإذا أخذ مع قيد الحدوث لم يكن لهذا المجموع إمكان أصلاً، لأن الحدوث أمر اعتباري يستحيل وجوده فالمجموع من حيث هو ممتنع لا ممكن. فإن قلت : نحن نأخذ ذات الحادث لا وحده بل مع الحدوث، على أنه قيد لا جزء . . ونقول : إنه ممتنع في الأزل وممكن فيما لا يزال . قلت : الإمكان الذاتي معتبر بالقياس إلى ذات الشيء من حيث هو، فإن أخذ ذات الحادث وحده، أو ذات
الاتصاف بالوجود إذ لو تحقق المنع من الاتصاف بالوجود في الجزء لم يكن عدم المنع عن قبول الوجود مستمراً، لأن قبول الوجود هو الاتصاف به.
قوله : (بل جاز اتصافه إلخ لأن عدم المنع عن الاتصاف يستلزم جواز الاتصاف، فيجوز الاتصاف بالوجود في كل جزء منها، بأن يكون كل جزء منها ظرفاً للاتصاف . قوله : ( لا بد له فقط بل ومعاً أيضاً لأن كل جزء منها مع قطع النظر عن جزء آخر يكون ظرفاً للاتصاف، على ما هو معنى الكل الإفرادي، فيكون شاملاً للاتصاف بطريق البدلية، بأن يكون كل جزء بدلاً عن الآخر في الاتصاف، وللاتصاف بطريق المعية بأن يكون كل جزء مجتمعاً مع جزء آخر في الاتصاف، فيكون الاتصاف بالوجود حاصلاً في جميعها، وهو الاتصاف بالوجود المستمر فجوازه جوازه. وبما حررنا ظهر الملازمات في جميع الشرطيات واندفع المنوع التي أوردها الناظرون، فلا حاجة إلى الإطناب ولا يرد عليه النقص بالحروف الآنية، ولا المنع بجعلها سنداً على ما ،وهم لأن أزليتها بالنظر إلى ماهياتها ممكنة وإن كانت ممتنعة بالنظر إلى وصف لازم لذاتها، أعني كونها آنية فإنه لا تنافي بين إمكان الشيء بالقياس إلى ذاته، وامتناعه بالقياس إلى أمر لازم لذاته، فتدبر
قوله : ( نعم إلخ) تقرير لما سبق، وجواب عن التشكيك المذكور بطريق آخر بمنع أن أزلية الحوادث غير ممكنة في الأزل؛ لأن الامتناع بسبب الحدوث امتناع ،بالغير، وهو لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي .
يقول : كما أنه لا يجوز اتصاف الأمر الغير القار بالوجود في أجزاء الأزل معاً، ليس له أيضاً إمكان مستمر فيها .
قوله : نعم ربما امتنعت إلخ) جواب عن سؤال مقدر ، وبه يخرج الجواب عن التشكيك ابتداء . قوله: (قلت : الإمكان الذاتي إلخ) قيد الإمكان بالذاتي احترازاً عن الإمكان الاستعدادي، لا عن الإمكان بالغير.
Then what the verifying commentator mentioned is refuted in general by time and motion; because what is possible in existence from them according to the verifiers is the flowing now and motion in the sense of intermediateness, and they are two settled things with no parts at all, so their possibility is eternal and their eternity is possible, indeed actual according to the philosophers. As for motion in the sense of traversing and non-settled time, they have no possibility at all, nor in the category of action and passion, for the commentator established the proof of their impossibility and did not answer it; perhaps they are non-existent according to him; this is the school of later verifiers. Rather, the instantaneous letters that occur to sounds when they are cut off, like the occurrence of the now to time and the point to the line, for they have stated and the commentator has also stated that they have no existence except in the instant of their occurrence, so they have the eternity of possibility without the possibility of eternity. And the statement that their eternity is possible in view of their essence and quiddity, and the impossibility in view of the other, meaning existence in the first time, is not to be heeded; because this other is realized on the assumption of the continuation of their existence, so if their quiddities require passing away after existence, they cannot have continuance in themselves, decisively, as is not hidden from the contemplative. Unless it is permissible that the non-imagination of their continuance is due to something external to their quiddities, such that you may make the image of the refutation a support for prevention, and it is possible to extricate from the refutation by preventing the possibility of something non-settled. And its clarification is that the commentator is now in the process of repelling what the people mentioned from their statement: the eternity of possibility does not entail the possibility of eternity, and answering the doubt concerning their statement: possibility is necessary for the quiddity of the possible, so he is by this research supporting the doubt; so the eternity of possibility of every possible has not been established, and there is no doubt that the arrival of the refutation is dependent on establishing the eternity of possibility for the non-settled thing, so the disputant has that...
From them, rather it is permissible for it to be characterized by it in each of them, not only as a substitute, but also together. And the permissibility of its being characterized by it in each of them together is the possibility of its being characterized by continuous existence in all parts of eternity with respect to its essence, so the eternity of possibility entails the possibility of eternity. Yes, perhaps eternity is prevented due to another, and that does not contradict essential possibility. For example, an occurrence (hadith) can be eternal with respect to its essence as such, and is impossible if the occurrence is taken as restricted by its temporality; so the essence of the occurrence as such its possibility is eternal, and its eternity is also possible. And if taken with the condition of temporality, this composite has no possibility at all, because temporality is an adventitious thing whose existence is impossible, so the composite as such is impossible, not possible. For if you say: we take the essence of the occurrence not alone but with temporality, as a condition not a part... and we say: it is impossible in eternity and possible in what is not yet. I say: essential possibility is considered with respect to the essence of the thing as such, for if the essence of the occurrence is taken alone, or the essence...
Being characterized by existence, for if prevention from being characterized by existence were realized in the part, then the absence of prevention from accepting existence would not be continuous, because accepting existence is being characterized by it.
His saying: (rather it is permissible for it to be characterized etc.) because the absence of prevention from being characterized entails the permissibility of being characterized, so it is permissible to be characterized by existence in every part of them, such that every part is a locus of characterization. His saying: (not only as a substitute but also together) because every part of them, irrespective of another part, is a locus of characterization, according to the meaning of the individual whole, so it includes characterization by way of substitution, such that each part is a substitute for another in characterization, and characterization by way of togetherness, such that each part is combined with another part in characterization, so characterization by existence occurs in all of them, which is characterization by continuous existence, so its permissibility is its permissibility. And by what we have explained, the entailments in all conditionals become manifest, and the preventions that the disputants mentioned are repelled, so there is no need for prolixity. And the objection from instantaneous letters does not apply, nor the prevention by making them a support for what they imagined, because their eternity with respect to their quiddities is possible, even if they are impossible with respect to a description necessary to their essence, namely being instantaneous. For there is no contradiction between the possibility of a thing with respect to its essence and its impossibility with respect to something necessary to its essence, so ponder.
His saying: (Yes etc.) is a confirmation of what preceded, and an answer to the mentioned doubt by another way, by preventing that the eternity of events is impossible in eternity; because the impossibility due to temporality is an impossibility by another, and it does not contradict essential possibility.
He says: Just as it is not permissible for the non-settled thing to be characterized by existence in parts of eternity together, it also does not have continuous possibility in them.
His saying: (Yes, perhaps it is prevented etc.) is an answer to an implied question, and by it the answer to the doubt emerges initially. His saying: (I said: essential possibility etc.) restricts possibility to essential possibility to avoid the sense of dispositional possibility, not possibility by another.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer sequence. The objection is raised that the earlier proof is refuted by time and motion, because certain entities (like the flowing now and motion as intermediation) are settled and have no parts, so they have eternal possibility and their eternity is actual. Other entities (traversing motion and non-settled time) are impossible, and the commentator did not answer this, perhaps because he denies them. Also instantaneous letters (huruf aniyya) only exist in the instant of their occurrence, so they have the eternity of possibility but not the possibility of eternity. The author responds by distinguishing essential possibility from accidental impossibility. He explains that even if an entity like an occurrence (hadith) is impossible in eternity when taken with the condition of temporality, its essence alone has eternal possibility. The key point is that possibility with respect to the essence does not contradict impossibility due to an external condition or a necessary attribute (like being instantaneous). The commentator's remarks reinforce this: the eternity of events is not impossible in eternity because the impossibility is by another (bi al-ghayr), not by essence. Thus essential possibility (imkan dhati) remains unaffected. The passage concludes that there is no contradiction between the possibility of a thing in itself and its impossibility due to something necessary to its essence.

Key Terms
أزلية الإمكان
إمكان الأزلية
إمكان ذاتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal possibility always entails possibility of eternity without exception.
Correction: The passage shows it holds for the essence but can be blocked by external conditions like necessary attributes.

Checkpoint

A) Necessity of existence.
B) Possibility of eternity for the essence.
C) Actual existence in eternity.
D) Impossibility of temporality.

Key Takeaway
Eternal possibility entails possibility of eternity only for the essence, not for a thing as modified by conditions.

Intrinsic Possibility and External Impossibility
Explains that external impossibility does not negate intrinsic possibility, with an objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between intrinsic possibility and external impossibility, and why external impossibility does not undermine intrinsic possibility.

Core Idea
External impossibility never cancels intrinsic possibility.

This passage from al-Sanusi tackles a subtle but critical point in kalam: the relationship between what is possible in itself and what is impossible due to external factors. Using the example of the contingent (al-hadith) and its temporality (al-huduth), the author argues that intrinsic possibility remains untouched by external impossibilities. An objection and its answer clarify the limits of 'possible by another'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Focus on the flow of the argument.
The passage contains a main claim, an example, an objection, and an answer.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the sentence stating that external impossibility does not negate intrinsic possibility. Note the key terms: الإمكان الذاتي and الامتناع بالغير.
3
Follow the example of the contingent
See how the author applies the claim to the contingent (الحادث) and its temporality (الحدوث). Understand the difference between taking the essence alone and the composite.
Temporality is an اعتباري (relational) matter.
4
Understand the objection and answer
The objector suggests taking the essence with temporality as a qualification. The answer stresses that intrinsic possibility is relative to the essence alone.
The answer distinguishes between possible in itself and possible by another.
5
Reflect on the 'secret'
Read the concluding reasoning about necessity/impossibility by another only affecting the possible. Understand why 'possibility by another' is not admissible.
This reinforces the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعم ربما امتنعت الأزلية بسبب الغير، وذلك لا ينافي الإمكان الذاتي، مثلاً الحادث يمكن أزليته بالنظر إلى ذاته من حيث هو، ويمتنع إذا أخذ الحادث مقيداً بحدوثه فذات الحادث من حيث هو إمكانه أزلي، وأزليته ممكنة أيضاً، وإذا أخذ مع قيد الحدوث لم يكن لهذا المجموع إمكان أصلاً، لأن الحدوث أمر اعتباري يستحيل وجوده فالمجموع من حيث هو ممتنع لا ممكن. فإن قلت: نحن نأخذ ذات الحادث لا وحده بل مع الحدوث، على أنه قيد لا جزء، ونقول: إنه ممتنع في الأزل وممكن فيما لا يزال. قلت: الإمكان الذاتي معتبر بالقياس إلى ذات الشيء من حيث هو، فإن أخذ ذات الحادث وحده، أو ذات المجموع، فقد عرفت حالهما. وإن أخذ ذات الحادث وحده، أو ذات الحادث مقيداً بقيد خارجي، لم يتصور هناك إمكان ذاتي، إذ ليس لنا ممكن بالغير على قياس الواجب أو الممتنع بالغير والسر فيه أن الوجوب والامتناع بالغير إنما يعرضان للممكن، ولا استحالة فيه، لأن الممكن هو الذي لا يقتضي الوجود والعدم، ونسبته إليهما على سواء بالنظر إلى ذاته فإذا وجد علة أحد طرفيه فوجب به وامتنع الطرف الآخر لم يضر ذلك في استواء نسبتهما إلى ذاته. وأما الإمكان بالغير فلا يجوز عروضه.
Yes, perhaps eternity is prevented due to another (bi-sabab al-ghayr), and that does not negate intrinsic possibility (al-imkan al-dhati). For example, the contingent (al-hadith) can be eternal by consideration of its essence in itself (min haythu huwa), and it is impossible if the contingent is taken as qualified by its temporality (muqayyadan bi-huduthihi). So the essence of the contingent in itself has its possibility eternal, and its eternity is also possible. And if it is taken with the qualification of temporality, this composite has no possibility at all, because temporality is a relational matter (amr i'tibari) whose existence is impossible, so the composite in itself is impossible, not possible. If you say: We take the essence of the contingent not alone but with temporality, as a qualification not a part, and we say: It is impossible in pre-eternity (al-azal) and possible in what is not yet (ma la yazal). I say: Intrinsic possibility is considered relative to the essence of the thing in itself. For if the essence of the contingent is taken alone, or the essence of the composite, you have known their states. And if the essence of the contingent is taken alone, or the essence of the contingent qualified by an external qualification, no intrinsic possibility is conceived there, because we have no possible by another (mumkin bi'l-ghayr) analogous to the necessary by another (wajib bi'l-ghayr) or the impossible by another (mumtani' bi'l-ghayr). The secret of it is that necessity and impossibility by another only occur to the possible (al-mumkin), and there is no impossibility in it, because the possible is that which does not necessitate existence or non-existence, and its relation to both is equal by consideration of its essence. So when a cause of one of its two sides is found, it becomes necessary by it and the other side becomes impossible; that does not harm the equality of their relation to its essence. As for possibility by another (al-imkan bi'l-ghayr), its occurrence is not permissible.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is an argument and objection-answer sequence. The author first asserts that external impossibility does not negate intrinsic possibility. He gives the example of the contingent (al-hadith): by its essence alone, it is possible for it to be eternal, but when considered with its temporality (huduth), the composite becomes impossible because temporality is a relational attribute that cannot exist as a real part. Then an objector says: We take the contingent's essence together with its temporality as a qualification, not a part, and we claim it is impossible in pre-eternity but possible in the future. The answer distinguishes intrinsic possibility: it is relative to the essence alone. If you take the essence alone or the composite, you know the result. If you take the essence alone or qualified by an external qualification, intrinsic possibility is not conceived because there is no 'possible by another' analogous to 'necessary by another' or 'impossible by another'. The reasoning is that necessity and impossibility by another only affect the possible (which is intrinsically neutral). Finding a cause for one side does not negate the intrinsic equality. Therefore, 'possibility by another' (imkan bi'l-ghayr) is not admissible for the intrinsically possible, as it would imply a change in the essence's neutrality.

Key Terms
الإمكان الذاتي
الامتناع بالغير
الحدوث
الحادث
الأزلية
الإمكان بالغير
الوجوب بالغير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think that if something is temporally impossible (e.g., the contingent being eternal), then it is also intrinsically impossible.
Correction: The passage shows that external impossibility (due to a qualification like temporality) does not negate the intrinsic possibility of the essence in itself. The essence of the contingent remains possible even if its eternity is impossible due to its temporality.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the composite of the contingent's essence and its temporality impossible?
A) Because temporality is a real part of the essence.
B) Because temporality is a relational matter whose existence is impossible.
C) Because the essence alone is impossible.
D) Because the contingent cannot be eternal.

Key Takeaway
Intrinsic possibility is about the essence alone; external impediments do not affect it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own life, do you define yourself by your past (like the qualification of temporality) and conclude that change is impossible? How does this lesson challenge you to see your essence as still intrinsically open to Allah's power?
?
Are there areas where you treat external circumstances as if they cancel your intrinsic capacity for good? What would it look like to act on the belief that no external impossibility reduces what you are in your essence before Allah?
?
The author denies 'possibility by another' because possibility is tied to essence alone. In your relationship with Allah, do you sometimes think your ability to repent or draw near depends on something external—like your current state or past—rather than on the intrinsic possibility of your soul? Will you start acting on that intrinsic possibility today?

Refuting Derived Possibility for the Intrinsically Possible
Presents and refutes a proof that al-imkan bi'l-ghayr cannot apply to the possible in itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that al-imkan bi'l-ghayr (possibility by another) cannot apply to something that is intrinsically possible (mumkin bi'l-dhat), and why the attempt to salvage it fails.

Core Idea
Derived possibility cannot apply to the intrinsically possible because it would cause an inversion of its nature.

This lesson presents a intricate theological argument from al-‘Aqā’id al-‘Aḍudiyya. The author claims that if something is possible in itself, it cannot also receive possibility from an external cause. A proof is given, an objection is raised, and a response is analyzed. By the end, you will see why a single essence cannot have two distinct relations of possibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the technical terms: الإمكان بالغير, الممكن بالذات, الانقلاب.
2
Understand the Proof
Identify the proof: if derived possibility were allowed, removing the cause would remove possibility, turning the thing into necessary or impossible—an inversion.
3
Examine the Objection
Consider the objection: the cause might be necessary (wajib), so it cannot be removed, thus avoiding inversion.
4
Analyze the Refutation
The commentator points out that only the derived possibility is removed, not the intrinsic one. But this fails because a single essence cannot have multiple relations of possibility.
Focus on why the commentator dismisses the response as invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وأما الإمكان بالغير فلا يجوز عروضه للممكن بالذات) قد يستدل على ذلك بوجه آخر، وهو أنه لو جاز لارتفع الإمكان بارتفاع ذلك الغير فلا يكون ممكناً في ذاته، بل واجباً أو ممتنعاً، ويلزم الانقلاب، ورد بجواز كون ذلك الغير واجباً، فلا يمكن ارتفاعه المفضي إلى ارتفاع الإمكان المفضي إلى الانقلاب. قال الشارح في حواشي التجريد: على التسليم، وفيه بحث؛ لأن اللازم ارتفاع إمكانه الحاصل من الغير لا ارتفاع إمكانه المستند إلى ذاته قبل، وليس بشيء، لأن استواء الوجود والعدم بالقياس إلى ذات واحدة لا يتصور فيه تعدد أصلاً.
His saying: (And as for possibility by another (al-imkan bi'l-ghayr), its occurrence for that which is possible in itself (al-mumkin bi'l-dhat) is not permissible.) This may be argued by another proof: that if it were permissible, then possibility would be lifted by the lifting of that other (al-ghayr), so it would not be possible in itself, but rather necessary or impossible, and an inversion (inqilab) would follow. It was objected that that other might be necessary, so its lifting which would lead to the lifting of possibility, which leads to inversion, is not possible. The commentator (al-sharih) said in the margins of al-Tajrid: Accepting that, but there is a discussion; because what necessarily follows is the lifting of its possibility obtained from the other, not the lifting of its possibility based on its essence before. And that is nothing, because the equality of existence and non-existence relative to one essence cannot be conceived with multiplicity at all.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation. The author quotes a statement: 'As for possibility by another (al-imkan bi'l-ghayr), it is not permissible for the possible in itself.' Then a proof is given: if such possibility were permissible, then when the other (the cause) is removed, the possibility would be removed, causing the thing to become necessary or impossible—an inversion from its intrinsic nature. An objection is raised: the other might be necessary (wajib), so its removal is impossible, thus the inversion is avoided. The commentator (sharih) in his notes on al-Tajrid responds: even if we accept that, there is a problem; because what would be removed is the possibility derived from the other, not the possibility based on the essence itself. This response is dismissed as invalid, because the equality of existence and non-existence relative to a single essence cannot be subject to multiplicity—i.e., you cannot have two distinct relations of possibility for the same essence. Thus the original proof stands, and imkan bi'l-ghayr is impossible.

Key Terms
الإمكان بالغير
الممكن بالذات
الانقلاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that derived possibility (al-imkan bi'l-ghayr) is a valid concept for intrinsically possible things, similar to derived necessity (al-wujub bi'l-ghayr).
Correction: This passage shows that derived possibility cannot apply to the intrinsically possible because it would lead to an inversion of the thing's nature, and a single essence cannot have multiple states of possibility.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the defense that the 'other' could be necessary, thus avoiding inversion?
A) Because if the other is necessary, then the thing would be necessary by it, not possible.
B) Because what is lifted is only the possibility from the other, not the intrinsic possibility, but the intrinsic equality cannot be multiple.
C) Because the proof requires that the other be contingent.
D) Because the inversion would still occur if the other is necessary.

Key Takeaway
The argument shows that al-imkan bi'l-ghayr cannot coexist with intrinsic possibility because a single essence cannot have multiple states of possibility.

The Root of the Eternity Dispute: God's Agency Type
Al-Razi traces the eternity dispute to the nature of divine agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi traces the disagreement about the world's eternity to a more fundamental question about the nature of God's agency—whether He acts by necessity or by free choice.

Core Idea
The eternity debate depends entirely on whether God creates by necessity or by choice.

Al-Razi cuts through the long debate between philosophers and theologians. Both sides agree the world is attributed to God. The real divide is simple: is God an agent by essence (like a cause that necessarily produces its effect) or a free agent who intends and chooses? This passage shows that if both sides agreed on the type of agency, they would automatically agree on the world's status.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two positions
The passage opens with the philosophers' view: God is a necessitator (mūjib bi al-dhāt), so He must produce an eternal world. The theologians disagree.
Notice that both sides accept the world is from God.
2
Identify the two points of agreement
Al-Razi says both groups agree that an effect can be attributed to a necessary cause if its effect endures, and both agree that a free agent cannot produce an eternal effect because intention precedes the action.
This is crucial for understanding the logical structure.
3
Pinpoint the real dispute
The passage concludes that the real dispute is about the kind of agency, not about whether the world is attributable to God. If all agreed God is a necessitator, all would affirm eternity; if all agreed He is free, all would affirm temporal origination.
This is the key takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحكماء إنما أسندوه أي القديم الذي هو العالم على رأيهم (إلى الفاعل) الذي هو الله تعالى ( لاعتقادهم أنه تعالى ( موجب بالذات)، لا فاعل بالاختيار، ولو اعتقدوا كونه مختاراً لم يذهبوا إلى قدم العالم المستند إليه. والمتكلمون لوسلموا كونه تعالى موجباً بالذات (لم يمنعوا استناده) أي استناد القديم (إِليه) تعالى. فالحاصل جواز استناده إلى () الفاعل (الموجب اتفاقاً) من الفريقين ( بأن يدوم أثره ) أي أثر الموجب ( بدوام ذاته، فيكون كلاهما استناد أحدهما إلى الآخر، ويمتنع استناده) أي وامتناع استناده (إلى الفاعل المختار اتفاقاً منهما أيضاً؛ ) لأن فعل المختار مسبوق بالقصد إلى الإيجاد ) دون فعل الموجب إذ لا قصد له ( وأنه) أي القصد إلى الإيجاد مقارن للعدم)، أي لعدم ما قصد إيجاده (ضرورة)، فإن القصد إلى إيجاد الموجود ممتنع بديهة ( فنزاعهم ) في قدم العالم وحدوثه مع كونه مستنداً إلى الله تعالى اتفاقاً، ليس مبنياً على أن الحكماء جوزوا استناد القديم إلى الفاعل فحكموا بأن العالم قديم ومع قدمه مستند إليه تعالى، وأن المتكلمين لم يجوزوا استناد القديم إلى الفاعل فحكموا بأن العالم حادث مستند إليه تعالى، بل هذا النزاع بينهم ) عائد إلى كون الفاعل) الموجد للعالم موجباً أو مختاراً)، حتى لو اتفقوا كلهم على أنه موجب، أو على أنه مختار لاتفقوا على قدم العالم على التقدير الأول، وعلى حدوثه على التقدير الثاني هكذا ذكره الإمام الرازي
The philosophers only attributed it, i.e., the Eternal which is the world according to their view, to the Agent who is God Most High, because they believe that He Most High is an agent by essence (mūjib bi al-dhāt), not a free agent (fā‘il bi al-ikhtiyār). If they had believed He is free, they would not have gone to the eternity of the world attributed to Him. And if the theologians had accepted that He Most High is an agent by essence, they would not have prevented its attribution, i.e., the attribution of the Eternal to Him Most High. So the conclusion is: the permissibility of attributing it to the agent who is the necessitator (al-mūjib) is agreed upon by both groups, because its effect endures with the endurance of His essence, so each is the attribution of one to the other. And its impermissibility, i.e., the impermissibility of attributing it to the free agent, is also agreed upon by both; because the act of the free agent is preceded by the intention (al-qaṣd) to bring into existence, unlike the act of the necessitator, as he has no intention. And that intention to bring into existence is concomitant with non-existence, i.e., with the non-existence of what is intended to be brought into existence—necessarily, because the intention to bring into existence what already exists is intrinsically impossible. So their dispute concerning the eternity of the world and its temporal origination (ḥudūth), while it is attributed to God Most High by agreement, is not based on the fact that the philosophers permitted the attribution of the Eternal to the Agent and thus judged the world eternal and despite its eternity attributed to Him, and that the theologians did not permit the attribution of the Eternal to the Agent and thus judged the world temporally originated and attributed to Him Most High. Rather, this dispute among them goes back to whether the agent who brings the world into existence is a necessitator (mūjib) or a free agent (mukhtār), such that if they all agreed that He is a necessitator, or that He is free, they would agree on the eternity of the world in the first case, and on its temporal origination in the second case. This is what Imam al-Razi mentioned.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal analysis by Imam al-Razi (as quoted by the author) of the root cause of the disagreement between philosophers (ḥukamā') and theologians (mutakallimūn) over whether the world is eternal (qadīm) or temporally originated (ḥādith), despite both groups agreeing that the world is attributed to God Most High as its agent. The passage begins by explaining why philosophers claim the world is eternal: they believe God is an agent by necessity (mūjib bi al-dhāt), not a free agent (fā‘il bi al-ikhtiyār). If they believed He was free, they would not have affirmed the world's eternity. Conversely, if theologians accepted that God is an agent by necessity, they would not deny that the eternal world (a qadīm) could be attributed to Him. Both groups agree that an effect can be attributed to a necessitating cause if the effect endures as long as the cause endures—this is the basis of the philosophers' claim. However, both also agree that a free agent cannot produce an eternal effect, because a free agent's act is preceded by an intention (qaṣd) to bring about something that does not yet exist; intending to bring about an already-existing thing is impossible. Therefore, the real dispute is not about whether the world, however it stands, can be attributed to God—since all agree it is attributed to Him. Instead, the dispute is about the nature of God's agency: is He a necessitator (mūjib) or a free agent (mukhtār)? If all agreed He is a necessitator, they would all say the world is eternal; if all agreed He is free, they would all say the world is temporally originated. Thus al-Razi argues that the question of the world's eternity versus temporal origination is entirely dependent on the prior question of whether God acts by necessity or by free choice.

Key Terms
موجب بالذات
فاعل بالاختيار
قصد إلى الإيجاد
قدم العالم
حدوث العالم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the dispute is about whether the world needs a creator at all.
Correction: The passage clearly states both groups agree the world is attributed to God. The real dispute is about the type of divine agency.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi in this passage, what do both philosophers and theologians agree upon?
A) That the world is eternal
B) That the world is temporally originated
C) That an effect can be attributed to a necessary agent if it endures with His essence
D) That God is a free agent

Key Takeaway
The dispute over the world's eternity is not about whether God created the world, but about whether His agency is necessary or free.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own life, do you tend to assume God's actions are mechanical (like a necessitator) or deeply personal (like a free agent)? How would your reliance on Him change if you truly internalized that He chose to create you and intervene in your life by His own free will, not by necessity? What can you do this week to remind yourself of that personal agency?
?
Al-Razi shows that the entire worldview hinges on whether God acts by essence or by choice. Have you ever considered that if God were a necessitator, your existence would be forced upon Him, but because He is a free agent, He decided to create you out of love and wisdom? How does that truth impact your sense of purpose and your relationship with Him?
?
If the dispute over the world's eternity is rooted in the nature of divine agency, what does that tell you about the importance of understanding God's attributes? Are you content with a shallow understanding of who God is, or are you willing to dive deeper into these discussions to strengthen your faith? What is one step you can take today to learn more about God's names and attributes?
